  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer13608351296060809341">Destroy Me tells the events between Shatter Me and Unravel Me from Warner's point of view. Even though Juliette shot him in order to escape, Warner can't stop thinking about her--and he'll do anything to get her back. But when the Supreme Commander of The Reestablishment arrives, he has much different plans for Juliette. Plans Warner cannot allow.<br/><br/>Fracture Me is told from A</span>
  <span id="freeText13608351296060809341" style="display:none">Destroy Me tells the events between Shatter Me and Unravel Me from Warner's point of view. Even though Juliette shot him in order to escape, Warner can't stop thinking about her--and he'll do anything to get her back. But when the Supreme Commander of The Reestablishment arrives, he has much different plans for Juliette. Plans Warner cannot allow.<br /><br />Fracture Me is told from Adam's perspective and bridges the gap between Unravel Me and Ignite Me. As the Omega Point rebels prepare to fight the Sector 45 soldiers, Adam's more focused on the safety of Juliette, Kenji, and his brother. The Reestablishment will do anything to crush the resistance... including killing everyone Adam cares about.<br /><br />Perfect for fans of Tahereh Mafi's New York Times bestselling Shatter Me trilogy, this also features an exclusive look into Juliette's journal and a preview of Ignite Me, the third installment of the series.</span>

<a href="/questions/908603-does-anyone-know-a-website-where-you-can">Does anyone know a website where you can read free books without an account or anything?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_908603'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18481271-unite-me">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/50938238-shannon-fay"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1451740716i/50938238._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/50938238-shannon-fay">Shannon Fay</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">i mean, it's not REALLY an account, but if you get a library card, you can read TONS of books for free from your local library system, as physical boo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">i mean, it's not REALLY an account, but if you get a library card, you can read TONS of books for free from your local library system, as physical books, ebooks or even listen to audiobooks, all for free, and all you need is proof of address/residence to get a library card at your local library.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/45597324-kylie-george">Kylie George</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's basically a compilation of all of her journal entries from the books, along with a lot more. It's really beautifully written. There's repetition,<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's basically a compilation of all of her journal entries from the books, along with a lot more. It's really beautifully written. There's repetition, crossed out lines and other elements that make it an interesting read. I liked the journal part of the novella the best. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421648567" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17776568244138856905"><b>
  <blockquote>“Because these words I write down are the only proof I have that I'm still alive” </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490183036i/22288512._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Well ... This book was quite enjoyable for me. Since Warner is my main ship, I adored every minute I read his stories which surprised me no end about how deep his character is. That being said, Warner compared to Adam made me see the big differences even though I shipped Adam so hard in Shatter Me. Warner hasn't judged Juliette by her power or capability, being totally in love with a girl whose power is lethal.</span>

  <blockquote>“Because these words I write down are the only proof I have that I'm still alive” </blockquote>

This book was quite enjoyable for me. Since Warner is my main ship, I adored every minute I read his stories which surprised me no end about how deep his character is. That being said, Warner compared to Adam made me see the big differences even though I shipped Adam so hard in Shatter Me. Warner hasn't judged Juliette by her power or capability, being totally in love with a girl whose power is lethal. Adam is too good to be true, suffice to say, he could be with Juliette if there aren't those problems throwing in his face in Unravel Me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But I know that Mafi intended to make Warner a hero of this series. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Unite Me includes two stories of Adam and Warner. You won't see much about their lives in this one, alas they're just short stories completing the gaps between book one and two and book two and three.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490183036i/22288514._SY540_.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490183036ra/22288513.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490183036ra/22288511.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490183036ra/22288510.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2924154084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2924154084" />
    <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52207144"><img alt="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568965358p2/52207144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2924154084?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" href="/user/show/52207144">♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=dystopia-and-utopian">dystopia-and-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2924154084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer412149105348720611">I usually don't enjoy novellas all that much. They usually bore me, still, I read them anyway because they are quick to read. I am so happy I read this.<br/><br/><u>
  <b>Destroy Me (Shatter Me #1.5) Warner's POV</b>
</u> ★★★★★<br/><br/><i>“Watching her talk to someone else made me crazy. I was jealous. Ridiculous. I wanted her to know me; I wanted her to talk to me. And I felt it then: this strange, inexplicable sense that she might be the only person in the world I could really care about.”</i><br/><br/>If I thought I was intrigued by Warner i</span>
  <span id="freeText412149105348720611" style="display:none">I usually don't enjoy novellas all that much. They usually bore me, still, I read them anyway because they are quick to read. I am so happy I read this.<br><br><u>
  <b>Destroy Me (Shatter Me #1.5) Warner's POV</b>
</u> ★★★★★<br><br><i>“Watching her talk to someone else made me crazy. I was jealous. Ridiculous. I wanted her to know me; I wanted her to talk to me. And I felt it then: this strange, inexplicable sense that she might be the only person in the world I could really care about.”</i><br><br>If I thought I was intrigued by Warner in Shatter Me, I have fallen so completely for him now. Just like I thought, there is just so much more to him then what meets the eye. He is not all malice and heartlessness, it's what he was taught and molded into. But if given the chance, people might just surprise you. I loved that we got a chance to be inside Warner's head. It's always refreshing when we get insight into another character's mind and a look into their soul. I love complex characters so much and I love Warner even MORE!!! :D <br><br>Warner... *sighhh<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479907533ra/21250424.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“This girl is destroying me. A girl who has spent the last year in an insane asylum. A girl who would try to shoot me dead for kissing her. A girl who ran off with another man just to get away from me. Of course, this is the girl I would fall for. I close a hand over my mouth. I am losing my mind.”</i> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521269490i/25226814._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>Fracture Me (Shatter Me #2.5) Adam's POV</b>
</u> ★★★<br><br><i>“All I can think is how horrible and beautiful it is, that our eyes blur the truth when we can't bear to see it.”</i><br><br><br>Ugh... I wonder how I ever like this guy? Seriously how?? Adam is so broody and is an annoyingly negative ass, who whines way to freaking much. He doesn't believe in anything, NOT in the people of Omega Point, NOT in their cause and he sure as HELL doesn't believe in Juliette! I can't stand how much he underestimates Juliette all the time, or the way he acts like she's a porcelain doll that can easily be broken, and the way he doubts the control of her powers and how deep down he's afraid of what her touch could do. I swear he acts as if he's better and could do a better job then everyone else and yet... he does nothing!! There are a few sad bits like the parts with Adam and his little brother James, and the loss of so many people and the loss of Omega Point. Things quickly go from bad to worse, and there were so much destruction and devastation in the wake of the battle against the Reestablishment. This really didn't do much for his character. My feelings for Adam aside, I am glad I read this because it was nice getting insight into what happened after Juliette was taken by Anderson's men but I wish it was in Kenji POV instead. I do NOT like him! Adam is all kinds of wrong for Juliette.<br><br><i>“Every day we feel further apart. And sometimes I think the harder I try to hold on, the more she tries to break away.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521078904ra/25215195.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="412149105348720611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365171093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12350388492201593584">This really made me love Aaron and dislike Adam. Mostly the latter because now I truly understand how he was holding Juliette back. He basically thought of her as a wounded dog he needed to protect. It was always "Juliette's gonna cry" "Juliette will probably puke" and "Juliette is locked inside her own world today" and the love Aaron has for her is nowhere near Adam's heart or mind. <br/><br/>This is a must-read for the trilogy to be whole.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3619970-holly-holly-s-reading-hollow?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3619970-holly-holly-s-reading-hollow?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3619970-holly-holly-s-reading-hollow?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3619970-holly-holly-s-reading-hollow?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3619970-holly-holly-s-reading-hollow?shelf=2014-march">2014-march</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3619970-holly-holly-s-reading-hollow?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872191901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16003860343641481333"><b>Thoughts on <i>Destroy Me</i>:</b><br/>I understand Warner more now. I don't think he is a monster, but as I remember some of the things he said to Juliette in Unravel Me, I still don't like him.<br/><br/><b>Thoughts on <i>Fracture Me</i>:</b><br/>I am so frustrated! Adam, what the heck?! Acting like Juliette's a burden, something to take care of because she can't take care of herself, instead of caring for her! Juliette's the weak link, Juliette's too trapped in her own head, Juliette can't protect herself...ugh!! I'm so peeved. This isn'</span>
  <span id="freeText16003860343641481333" style="display:none"><b>Thoughts on <i>Destroy Me</i>:</b><br />I understand Warner more now. I don't think he is a monster, but as I remember some of the things he said to Juliette in Unravel Me, I still don't like him.<br /><br /><b>Thoughts on <i>Fracture Me</i>:</b><br />I am so frustrated! Adam, what the heck?! Acting like Juliette's a burden, something to take care of because she can't take care of herself, instead of caring for her! Juliette's the weak link, Juliette's too trapped in her own head, Juliette can't protect herself...ugh!! I'm so peeved. This isn't the Adam I've grown to love! This sounds more like the Adam Warner imagines in his head, not the real one. I understand him doubting whether they should be together, with everything going on and Juliette breaking up with him but he's acting like he only loves her because she needs him, not because he needs and wants and loves her for who she is. I got the sense that he knows nothing about Juliette from this novella, which is not how I ever pictured him. Again, this is how Warner imagines Adam. Did Mafi do this on purpose? Make us turn away from Adam completely so everyone will be happy <s>when</s> if Warner and Juliette end up together?<br /><br />On the upside, I love James more and his nickname for Adam. I love Kenji and how he sees strength in Juliette but I also like him just because he's the best. He might be one of my favorite supporting characters ever. I liked seeing what Juliette is like from an outside perspective when she closes herself off and lives in her mind, and how some things trigger her to come back to life. It was interesting to learn that she actually does repeat her words out loud like how she does in her head.<br /><br /><b>Thoughts on Juliette's Journal:</b><br />We already get the chance to see most of her journal entries between <i>Shatter Me, Unravel Me,</i> and <i>Destroy Me</i>, but I liked seeing them all in one binding and simply rereading them all again. It's a very peculiar thing to be in Juliette's mind when she's at the lowest points of her life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16003860343641481333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2117831035?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Elaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Elaina" href="/user/show/54237690-sophie-elaina">Sophie Elaina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=novellas-and-short-stories">novellas-and-short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-paperbacks">owned-paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117831035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13057888905980710802">Destroy Me: 2.5/2.5<br/><br/>Destroy Me is and excellent addition to the Shatter Me series and I enjoyed the fact it delved in to Warner’s situation between Shatter Me and Unravel Me. It was great to see behind the scenes and see what his life is really like and Tahereh Mafi did a great job adding slightly more depth to Warner’s character development with this little novella. If you love Warner, you’ll get a lot of insight into his character especially if you have not yet read Ignite Me.<br/><br/>Fracture Me: 1/2.5</span>
  <span id="freeText13057888905980710802" style="display:none">Destroy Me: 2.5/2.5<br /><br />Destroy Me is and excellent addition to the Shatter Me series and I enjoyed the fact it delved in to Warner’s situation between Shatter Me and Unravel Me. It was great to see behind the scenes and see what his life is really like and Tahereh Mafi did a great job adding slightly more depth to Warner’s character development with this little novella. If you love Warner, you’ll get a lot of insight into his character especially if you have not yet read Ignite Me.<br /><br />Fracture Me: 1/2.5<br /><br />Fracture Me is from Adam's perspective and starts off close to the end of Unravel Me. It was great to finally read from Adam's perspective and get a better insight into him as a character. However he is a character I have disliked very much from the get go so I didn't particularly enjoy this. I found this novella to be pretty boring and wasn’t a necessary addition to the series.<br /><br />Overall Rating: 3.5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13057888905980710802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/980948394?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=read-it-and-weep">read-it-and-weep</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer980948394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer586913636005803045">Was reminded why I love t mafi so much. And those journal entries.... Sweet Jesus They're sad <br/><br/>First I would like to say that I'm writing this review for the whole Shatter Me series, and second that I never EVER write reviews... That being said here's my review of the shatter me series. <br/><br/>	Breathtaking, wonderful, stunning.... I could use any of those words to describe this series but they would all be understatement. <br/><br/>Mafi's writing is beyond refreshing and unique. It's something so hard to describ</span>
  <span id="freeText586913636005803045" style="display:none">Was reminded why I love t mafi so much. And those journal entries.... Sweet Jesus They're sad <br /><br />First I would like to say that I'm writing this review for the whole Shatter Me series, and second that I never EVER write reviews... That being said here's my review of the shatter me series. <br /><br />	Breathtaking, wonderful, stunning.... I could use any of those words to describe this series but they would all be understatement. <br /><br />Mafi's writing is beyond refreshing and unique. It's something so hard to describe or even put into words, and I know that my review wont do it true justice.<br /><br />I found myself drowning in her words and not wanting to come up for air. I wanted the waves of her writing to crash over me and pull me further and further out. I'm pretty sure I held my breath the whole time I was reading this series (which might I add I finished in less than two days).<br /><br />Since finishing this series I have found myself comparing any book I have read or am reading to it. Never has a writer made me fall so in love with characters and made me feel like whatever happened to them was happening to me. Her characters will steal your heart and soul. Juliette will make you feel empowered and brave. Adam will make you remember what love feels like. Warner will show you everything you secretly want and OH BOY WILL YOU WANT IT, and Kenji will be the friend you've always wanted.<br /><br />I could go on for <s>days</s>... <s>weeks</s>... no years about this book. I would go so into detail and fine tooth comb and break down every chapter if I could, but I wont because I would never want to tarnish, or give out any details to someone who hasn't had the chance to read this masterpiece, because that's what this series is. It's the Mona Lisa of ya novels. A slight mysterious smile that you can't turn away from. It makes you want to scream out loud and kiss Tahereh's forehead and thank her for writing something so on point. so on point. <br /><br />I could seriously keep going, but I'll spare you the novel of a review I could write and leave you with this.....<br />	You know how you meet someone with such passion for what they do and all you can think is "wow, this person was born to do this" <b>well Tahereh Mafi was meant to be a writer, and I'm SO very thankful that she is! Thanks for the permanent goose bumps, tears, laughs, and never ending book hang over that you have rewarded me with.I am forever in your debt. </b><br /><br />Read this review and other one our blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/">http://southernbredsouthernread.blogs...</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/941151937?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor Knight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor Knight" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight">Taylor Knight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer941151937" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1830829107574180102"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430692193ra/14748393.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>It'd had been so insanely long since I read this series that I wasn't sure if it was too late for me to read this book. I remember all the other books really well but I wasn't sure if it would be hard for me to get back into this series because it's been two years since I read Ignite Me. But I was very surprised to find how easily I got back into this world and the characters.<br/><br/>I loved Destroy Me so much. I love Warner so much and reading from his point of view was amazing. I felt like everything</span>
  <span id="freeText1830829107574180102" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430692193ra/14748393.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>It'd had been so insanely long since I read this series that I wasn't sure if it was too late for me to read this book. I remember all the other books really well but I wasn't sure if it would be hard for me to get back into this series because it's been two years since I read Ignite Me. But I was very surprised to find how easily I got back into this world and the characters.<br><br>I loved Destroy Me so much. I love Warner so much and reading from his point of view was amazing. I felt like everything was relevant to the overall series and really expanded on his character. Reading Destroy Me really revived all the feelings I have for this series. <br><br>I had a little more trouble with Fracture Me. After the second book, I really wasn't a fan of Adam and really grew to hate him. So reading from his perspective just as his character was starting to annoying me, it didn't do much for me. It was interesting but I didn't get what I got from Destroy Me. Maybe it's because I don't like Adam, but I felt like Fracture Me wasn't super relevant to the series. I don't know, if you're "Team Adam" you'll most likely love Fracture Me. I don't love Adam so I didn't love Fracture Me.<br></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2492284847" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2492284847" />
    <a title="Vaishali • [V.L. Book Reviews] ON A GR BREAK!" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break"><img alt="Vaishali • [V.L. Book Reviews] ON A GR BREAK!" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552133842p2/85343546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2492284847?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vaishali • [V.L. Book Reviews] ON A GR BREAK!" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vaishali • [V.L. Book Reviews] ON A GR BREAK!" href="/user/show/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break">Vaishali • [V.L. Book Reviews] ON A GR BREAK!</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/85343546-vaishali-v-l-book-reviews-on-a-gr-break?shelf=favourite-male-leads">favourite-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2492284847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9417091294342905799"><i>Rating: 4 stars </i><br/><br/><i>
  <b>‘Unite Me’</b>
</i> by <i>Tahereh Mafi</i> is a novella bind up, split into <i>
  <b>‘Fracture Me’</b>
</i> (From Adam’s point of view) and <i>
  <b>‘Destroy Me’</b>
</i> (Told from Warner’s point of view). The titles themselves are indicative enough, stressing how Juliette’s departure would affect both of these men; Losing Juliette for Warner would <i>destroy</i> him, but losing Juliette for Adam would only <i>fracture</i> him. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>This novella is very telling</b>
</i> – it highlights just how much and how far each of these men will go to f</span>
  <span id="freeText9417091294342905799" style="display:none"><i>Rating: 4 stars </i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘Unite Me’</b>
</i> by <i>Tahereh Mafi</i> is a novella bind up, split into <i>
  <b>‘Fracture Me’</b>
</i> (From Adam’s point of view) and <i>
  <b>‘Destroy Me’</b>
</i> (Told from Warner’s point of view). The titles themselves are indicative enough, stressing how Juliette’s departure would affect both of these men; Losing Juliette for Warner would <i>destroy</i> him, but losing Juliette for Adam would only <i>fracture</i> him. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>This novella is very telling</b>
</i> – it highlights just how much and how far each of these men will go to fight for Juliette’s love. Warner is ardent, unrelenting, unwavering and inexorable in his efforts to attain her. He will do despite the conditions. Adam is also ardent but only to an extent, and when a boundary presents itself, Juliette seems to become a secondary goal for him. His love seems provisional. Adam underestimates Juliette to such a degree, that when I read <i>
  <b>‘Fracture Me’</b>
</i>, it was more than surprising to see what he actually thought of her. Whereas Warner overestimates Juliette, believing in her capabilities to the ninth degree.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Fracture Me</b>
</i><br /><br />I was immensely bothered while reading Adam’s POV; it took me longer than a week to gain some kind of a reprieve from what I had just read. His take on Juliette was deprecatory; he has little to no belief in her, his thoughts rather insulting and critical, and such a contrast to what actually comes out of his mouth. I really didn’t want to dislike him, but after reading <i>
  <b>‘Fracture Me’</b>
</i> it was undeniably foreseeable. The only facet worth of value is Adam’s relationship with James, and his friendship with Kenji.<br /><br />I failed to find the symmetry and logic of his judgments when he was always the one to uplift Juliette, providing her with a base to realise her own strength. Adam’s affections seemed inadequate, and Juliette appeared to be a point of burden for him, only needing her because <i>he</i> desired the role as protector, and Juliette just happened to be the meek enabler. Adam is easily loved when we see him through Juliette’s eyes, but Adam from an objective outlook is vastly different. Adam’s psychology stems from his own personal ordeals, and I can’t help but wonder if Adam actually <i>loved</i> Juliette, or was his relationship with Juliette a product of his need to safeguard? <br /><br />Adam has always assumed the parent role for James and in James’s life, having a huge responsibility as a provider since he was a child, and it seemed that he assumed that same role with Juliette herself. I can wholly understand that James is his priority (as he should be), but he utterly and disappointingly gave up on Juliette not just as a potential lover, but as a friend. <br /><br />As impartial as I tried to be, I think the reason Adam affronted me to such as degree was because I’m invested in Juliette and her rehabilitation, and to poke around in Adam’s mind, examining his deplorable thoughts was more than dispiriting. Kenji fought much harder than Adam for his best friend. I wanted to believe that he was more than Warner’s opinion of him but that didn’t happen.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Destroy Me</b>
</i><br /><br />Onto greener pastures! <br /><br /><i>
  <b>‘Destroy Me’</b>
</i> is a fantastic addition to the series. Warner is exactly the laboured soul that Juliette thinks him to be. Her absence itself brings him physical and emotional pain; she simultaneously weakens and strengthens him. Reading this <i>
  <b>broke</b>
</i> my heart, seeing Warner's relationship with his dad <i>
  <b>broke</b>
</i> my heart, everything about him <i>
  <b>breaks</b>
</i> my heart. Tortured people always tend to be the most interesting just because they are so much more than they appear to be. Warner endures and survives because he has to, because he knows no other way, and he hadn’t truly lived until he met Juliette - she changed everything for him.<br /><br />His life is regimented, structured for organisation and compartmentalisation which opposes his chaotic thoughts and emotions – or rather that’s how he manages his highly feeling nature. He combats his pain and internal agony with uniformity and practiced control in his external environment. He very clearly struggles with mental health such as <i>
  <b>OCD, anxiety and PTSD,</b>
</i> and just like Juliette he has coping mechanisms in place to challenge his issues. Warner’s character is illustrative – he can still fight and survive despite the weight of his mental incapacities, and coping with them is attainable. <br /><br />Warner is alone in this world with the exception of Delalieu, (still don’t know how to pronounce his name) and Juliette is the one person who makes him feel less alone. His thought processes and mode of thinking is so divergent from Juliette’s own narrative. Though he is just as much at war with himself as Juliette is, he makes the best of what he was given. His thoughts are clear and concise, and I was glad to see the world through his eyes. The manner in which he thinks about Juliette is endearing and reassuring. How on Earth is it possible to not fall in love with him!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>'Unite Me'</b>
</i> was <i>fully satiating</i>, more so with the addition of Juliette’s beautifully written and poignant journal entries.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Favourite Quotes: </b>
</i><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br />
  <i>“She’s found the cracks in this cast I’m forced to wear every day, and it petrifies me. That this girl would know exactly how to shatter me.”<br /><br />“Torture is not torture when there’s any hope of relief.”<br /><br />“I grieve nothing. I take everything. It’s the only way I know how to live in this battered body. I empty my mind of the things that plague me and burden my soul, and I take all that I can from what little pleasantness comes my way.”<br /><br />“But there are some things I do not forgive. I don’t consider myself a moral man. I do not philosophize about life or bother with the laws and principles that govern most people. I do not pretend to know the difference between right and wrong. But I do live by a certain kind of code. And sometimes, I think, you have to learn how to shoot first.”<br /><br />“I’ve come to believe that the most dangerous man in the world is the one who feels no remorse. The one who never apologises and therefore seeks no forgiveness. Because in the end it is our emotions that make us weak, not our actions.”<br /><br />“I could live here, I think. Live where gravity does not know my name. Here I am unbound, untethered by the chains of this life. I am a different body, a different shell, and my weight is carried by the hands of friends.<br /><br />“I almost forget that she still hates me, despite how hard I’ve fallen for her. And I’ve fallen. So hard. I’ve hit the ground. Gone right through it. Never in my life have I felt this. Nothing like this. I’ve felt shame and cowardice, weakness and strength. I’ve known terror and indifference, self-hate and general disgust. I’ve seen things that cannot be unseen. And yet I’ve know nothing like this terrible, horrible, paralyzing feeling, I feel crippled. Desperate and out of control. And it keeps getting worse. Every day I feel sick. Empty and somehow aching. Love is a heartless bastard. I’m driving myself insane.”</i>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
    <br />
   <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1740294554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9970948703062361885"><br/><a href='http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br/><br/> THE WORLD: The world ruled by The Reestablishment. The world that went to hell and never recovered. The world that is corrupted as hell and people are back to being slaves. The world where some humans have extraordinary powers. The world of X-men? Well not exactly but close. Basically the world of Juliette and Warner. And Adam. Yeah, because he just cannot damn die for once.<br/><br/>CHARACTERS: So this book is actually two novellas and a diary of Juliette. Later is ju</span>
  <span id="freeText9970948703062361885" style="display:none"><br /><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br /><br /> THE WORLD: The world ruled by The Reestablishment. The world that went to hell and never recovered. The world that is corrupted as hell and people are back to being slaves. The world where some humans have extraordinary powers. The world of X-men? Well not exactly but close. Basically the world of Juliette and Warner. And Adam. Yeah, because he just cannot damn die for once.<br /><br />CHARACTERS: So this book is actually two novellas and a diary of Juliette. Later is just a collection of all little part of her diary we got to read in all three books. Now novellas...so Destroy Me is obviously about Warner and it is the time after the first book I think, basically when he finds her diary but before the third book happens. And the second novella is about Adam obviously, I expected to hate it because hello I hate Adam but yeah...actually it made a lot of sense. Adam is the jerk period. So yeaaaaah.....Warner. Oh boy oh boy how much I love him, getting to read from his POV, getting to know his thoughts....oh my.....*shivers*. I will never have enough of this man. Needless to say he is my most beloved male character of all times. Now Adam...have I already told you I hate him? Yeah? Well so I do hate him like hate hate. Jup, Adam should die. But let's talk about his novella. Basically it is after Juliette is taken and Adam goes with the group to the house. Where he completely forgets Juliette. You tell me he loved her and he had just different priorities? To hell with that, you do not just have different priorities when somebody you are ready to give your life for is taken away and probably is tortured or even killed. Ya just don't. So yeah, Adam just once again proved what a jerk he is. He doesn't care about Juliette. He is just pissed that she doesn't hate Warner like he does. Sick man, just sick. And then to make Juliette feel guilty about it....yeah *** you Adam.<br /><br />LOVE: There is no active Juliette so obviously there is no active love. Tho Destroy Me is very very passionate. You can see how things started...oh my....<br /><br />PLUS: These little details of Warner...his thoughts and sorta an open door for us to understand why he does what he does. This happened before book three where it all got black on white so it is just amazing to read more about him. I fish Tahereh Mafi would write more to this series.<br /><br />MINUS: I didn't really get the purpose of Juliette diary. I mean without context it is weird, her entries make no sense. Plus it is complete repeat. Weird.<br /><br />OVERALL: Needless to say I loved loved loved it! My first novellas to own and buy and so so worth it. Luw Warner to death!<br /><br /><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer785006074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8974100525785000687">I love the boys POV's. I read this after Ignite Me and I was so excited that there was more to learn. I left reviews on the boys titles, Destroy Me and Fracture Me. I also couldn't wait to read Juliette's diary. I know a lot of ppl dislike how Juliette's POV was written, with all of the metaphors and the crossed-out/unsaid words but I absolutely loved it. I think it is sensibly acceptable and plausible for a person who has been subjected to long-term horrific trauma, to then try and make detatch</span>
  <span id="freeText8974100525785000687" style="display:none">I love the boys POV's. I read this after Ignite Me and I was so excited that there was more to learn. I left reviews on the boys titles, Destroy Me and Fracture Me. I also couldn't wait to read Juliette's diary. I know a lot of ppl dislike how Juliette's POV was written, with all of the metaphors and the crossed-out/unsaid words but I absolutely loved it. I think it is sensibly acceptable and plausible for a person who has been subjected to long-term horrific trauma, to then try and make detatched sense of it, and how that reflects their vision of the world is completely reasonable. Well it made sense to me anyway. :)</span>

<div id="review_2043337840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043337840" />
    <a title="&amp;#x1d426;&amp;#x1d41a;&amp;#x1d42b;&amp;#x1d422;&amp;#x1d41a;⋆. · ⋆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60161669-x1d426-x1d41a-x1d42b-x1d422-x1d41a"><img alt="&amp;#x1d426;&amp;#x1d41a;&amp;#x1d42b;&amp;#x1d422;&amp;#x1d41a;⋆. · ⋆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552142200p2/60161669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043337840?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="&amp;#x1d426;&amp;#x1d41a;&amp;#x1d42b;&amp;#x1d422;&amp;#x1d41a;⋆. · ⋆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="&amp;#x1d426;&amp;#x1d41a;&amp;#x1d42b;&amp;#x1d422;&amp;#x1d41a;⋆. · ⋆" href="/user/show/60161669-x1d426-x1d41a-x1d42b-x1d422-x1d41a">&amp;#x1d426;&amp;#x1d41a;&amp;#x1d42b;&amp;#x1d422;&amp;#x1d41a;⋆. · ⋆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60161669-x1d426-x1d41a-x1d42b-x1d422-x1d41a?shelf=beloved-ones-forever">beloved-ones-forever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60161669-x1d426-x1d41a-x1d42b-x1d422-x1d41a?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043337840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7706131886223453881">This was so good. Warner my love. I have to say that this book is a wonderful addition to the series, it complements it perfectly. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Because only once the storm has passed, only once the tears have flooded the rivers and gorged the ground and washed away the dirt the debris the destruction and decay, only then—<br/>only then will the sun step outside<br/>smile to the sky<br/>and dare to shine.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Being able to see through Warner's eyes, read his thoughts and understand his feelings was such a beautiful, heart-ac</span>
  <span id="freeText7706131886223453881" style="display:none">This was so good. Warner my love. I have to say that this book is a wonderful addition to the series, it complements it perfectly. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Because only once the storm has passed, only once the tears have flooded the rivers and gorged the ground and washed away the dirt the debris the destruction and decay, only then—<br />only then will the sun step outside<br />smile to the sky<br />and dare to shine.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Being able to see through Warner's eyes, read his thoughts and understand his feelings was such a beautiful, heart-aching ride. Narrated during the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13455782.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a>, between the days where Juliette is starting a new life at Omega Point, we get a glimpse, a big opening, into Warner's life on base. It is like a tour inside his being, into how he little by little discovers how Juliette is changing everything he thought he had controlled. He is shattering, and his only salvation is having a piece of her in his hands: her notebook, her journal. Full of aching thoughts, that feel so much as his own, soon Warner discovers that the pain it causes him is all the effect of the love he now knows he feels for her.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“This girl is destroying me.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />We also get a glimpse into Adam's changing mind. He has changed a lot throughout the months in Omega Point, becoming an angry boy filled with doubts and lots of fear. He's only worry is protecting and keeping safe his little brother, James. He is so focused and obsessed in protecting him and Juliette, too; thinking that she is just a small girl incapable of fighting and surviving and protecting herself. Narrated in the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13104080.Unravel_Me__Shatter_Me___2_" title="Unravel Me (Shatter Me, #2) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Unravel Me</a>, Adam tells what happened in the battlefield and how he and Kenji managed to survived the massacre. We get a big glimpse into what he really thinks about everything, and how he only (somehow) wants to be safe and doesn't care about anything else, but him and his brother (and perhaps Juliette) being alive. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I like to keep most people out.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Finally, we are able to read what had Warner griping his heart inside his chest: Juliette's journal. Even as heartbreaking it is, understanding what she went to, the horrors and the grief and the pain, it is written in such a magical, beautiful way it is hypnotizing. Words that speak such truth in many ways, and maybe the stories of many people. I loved it very much.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Color your personality.<br />Shapes and sizes are variety.<br />Your heart is an anomaly.<br />Your actions<br />are<br />the<br />only<br />traces<br />you leave<br />behind.<br />Hang tight<br />Hold on<br />Look up<br />Stay strong<br />Hang on<br />Hold tight<br />Look strong<br />Stay up<br />One day I might break<br />One day I might<br />b r e a k<br />free.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7706131886223453881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2403343570" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2403343570" />
    <a title="Katherine Stargazing" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55879155-katherine-stargazing"><img alt="Katherine Stargazing" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532278452p2/55879155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2403343570?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine Stargazing" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine Stargazing" href="/user/show/55879155-katherine-stargazing">Katherine Stargazing</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55879155-katherine-stargazing?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55879155-katherine-stargazing?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55879155-katherine-stargazing?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55879155-katherine-stargazing?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55879155-katherine-stargazing?shelf=beautiful-cover">beautiful-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55879155-katherine-stargazing?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2403343570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7492344322967855878"><b>Destroy Me</b><br/><br/>This novel is written from Warner's POV. It begins after the scene where Warner got shot by Juliette and follows him through his recovery, his father's visit at the base in sector 45, his discovery of Juliette's journal to the iconic scene with the dog.<br/><br/>I LOVED reading his POV because he is such a complex character. He must not show emotions or mercy. He must act like a monster so everyone thinks he is one and fears him. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i> In the end it is our emotions that make us weak, not our actio</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText7492344322967855878" style="display:none"><b>Destroy Me</b><br /><br />This novel is written from Warner's POV. It begins after the scene where Warner got shot by Juliette and follows him through his recovery, his father's visit at the base in sector 45, his discovery of Juliette's journal to the iconic scene with the dog.<br /><br />I LOVED reading his POV because he is such a complex character. He must not show emotions or mercy. He must act like a monster so everyone thinks he is one and fears him. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> In the end it is our emotions that make us weak, not our actions. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Poor boy felt so mortified that a girl shot him for a kiss. Not <i>a girl</i>. The girl. The one he is not obsessed with but the one he fell for. The one he thinks about the whole day. Dreams about at night. <b>The one that destroyed him.</b> And when he found her journal he needed to be with her again so damn hard he couldn't resist and opened it. And read it.<br /><br /><b>Fracture Me</b><br /><br />The second novel is written from Adam's point of view. To be honest I expected to hate this novel. Though I liked Adam in Shatter Me, as the series went on he became one of the most annoying characters ever. <br />But I was surprised how much I enjoyed it. We follow him from the morning when everyone learns Warner escaped from the Point through the battle where the Point was bombarded and Juliette was kidnapped. <br /><br /><b>This is a story about brothers</b><br /><i>Adam (talking to James): I love you. You know that, right? You always come first. Everything I do is to take care of you. To protect you. To provide for you. It's you first. It's always you first and everyone else is second. And that's never going to change, okay?<br />James: Okay, Addie.</i><br /><br />Though Adam is often annoyed with James, angry whenever he calls him Addie and jealous when James complains that Kenji is never mean at him like Adam is, only in Fracture Me we can see how deep is Adam's love for him. For his little brother who means a world to him. He is terrified for his safety and he goes rigid when James wants to go with him to the battlefield. When Juliette gets kidnapped he and Kenji go right after her but meet other members of Point in the process and learn what is coming to the Point. Sure death for every single member the left behind, James being one of them. They speed back for <s>him</s> them when they hear the bombs and know it's over. That's when Adam almost lost his shit if James weren't running towards them terrified and crying. They don't go back for Juliette after that. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>I love Juliette. I really do. But part of me doesn't want to put James at risk again - on the run again - for a girl who broke up with me. A girl who walked away from us. I don't know if my allegiance is to James or Juliette. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />And here he goes <u>super annoying</u> again. If he doesn't choose James he is an as*hole. The end.<br /><br />PS: It was amazing to see Kenji again. I didn't even realize how much I missed him!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7492344322967855878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3372259244974162581"><b>[Updated 11/28]<b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385639082i/7192457._SY540_.jpg' width='440' height='660' alt='Fracture Me page 1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385639082i/7192458._SY540_.jpg' width='440' height='660' alt='Fracture Me page 2' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385639082i/7192459._SY540_.jpg' width='440' height='660' alt='Fracture Me page 3' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>What I love the most about this is that it's actually a print edition. I find it much more enjoyable and more emotional whenever I am actually holding the book itself. There are just some emotions that you can't truly feel and cherish when reading a story with Kindle, iBooks and whatnot. <br/><br/>It's also nice to know that I can have a print copy of the two novellas to display in my bookshelf....But this also means that we're already close to the ending of the Shatter Me trilogy.<br/><br/>I want to</b></b></span>
  <span id="freeText3372259244974162581" style="display:none"><b>[Updated 11/28]<b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385639082i/7192457._SY540_.jpg" width="440" height="660" alt="Fracture Me page 1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385639082i/7192458._SY540_.jpg" width="440" height="660" alt="Fracture Me page 2" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385639082i/7192459._SY540_.jpg" width="440" height="660" alt="Fracture Me page 3" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>What I love the most about this is that it's actually a print edition. I find it much more enjoyable and more emotional whenever I am actually holding the book itself. There are just some emotions that you can't truly feel and cherish when reading a story with Kindle, iBooks and whatnot. <br><br>It's also nice to know that I can have a print copy of the two novellas to display in my bookshelf....But this also means that we're already close to the ending of the Shatter Me trilogy.<br><br>I want to know what the cover would look like, though. A mixture of cover 1.1 and cover 2.1? Or maybe an image of two men, probably fighting or something. Can't wait to see it!<br><br>Lastly, I'm very curious as to what this bonus content is. Tahereh could put a picture of herself and that would very much count as bonus content for me. Maybe she'll also put information logs made by Adam? A mixture of Adam and Warner's extra contents in the novellas. But anyways, whatever this bonus content is I'm hoping it's something that won't make me regret reading Shatter Me. Because I wasn't supposed to read Shatter Me. I WAS NOT SUPPOSED TO FALL IN LOVE AND CRY OVER WARNER OKAY </b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3372259244974162581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iwb34UUH8m5kqCxsj+q4cP9aFACYtiyq26xvamW2wa6xIJ4z/lk7BsODmA14H7KvKQXzyFY7os2A0inbqPUzNA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p7JdXLQgqIoyNiSId2vu9XSOGxbmmx9+HFopOuHAnaSdlDSOD35h4pUdkOmAnuQqotH83igWkRlHJG+LLINvPg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14588154164475580325">Tahereh Mafi is the <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of the <i>Shatter Me</i> series. She was born in a small city somewhere in Connecticut and currently resides in Santa Monica, California with her husband, fellow author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3046613.Ransom_Riggs' title='Ransom Riggs' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ransom Riggs</a>. She can usually be found over-caffeinated and stuck in a book. <i>Shatter Me</i> is her first series, with television rights optioned by ABC Signature Studios; <i>Fur</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14588154164475580325" style="display:none">Tahereh Mafi is the <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of the <i>Shatter Me</i> series. She was born in a small city somewhere in Connecticut and currently resides in Santa Monica, California with her husband, fellow author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3046613.Ransom_Riggs" title="Ransom Riggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Ransom Riggs</a>. She can usually be found over-caffeinated and stuck in a book. <i>Shatter Me</i> is her first series, with television rights optioned by ABC Signature Studios; <i>Furthermore</i>, her first middle grade novel, is on shelves now, and <i>Whichwood</i>, its darker companion, will be on shelves November 14, 2017.</span>
